derivativesHigher-order derivatives ( parametric & vector-valued functions ) Polar curve differentiationThe big idea of differential calculus is the concept of the derivative , which essentially gives us the direction , or rate of change , of a function at any of its points . Learn all about derivatives and how to find them here.Practice for your next test51 exercises availableIntroduction to differential calculusWhat 's differential calculus all about ? An answer to this question lies just right here.Newton , Leibniz , and Usain Bolt Derivative as slope of curve Practice : Derivative as slope of curve Derivative & the direction of a function Practice : Derivative & the direction of a function Derivative notation review Derivative as slope of tangent lineOne way of thinking about the derivative ( of a function at a point ) is as the slope of the tangent line ( to the function 's graph at that point ) . Get comfortable with this approach here.Derivative as slope of tangent line Practice : Derivative as slope of tangent line Interpreting derivative challenge Derivative as instantaneous rate of changeOne way of thinking about the derivative is as instantaneous rate of change . This is quite incredible because rate of change is usually found over a period of time , and not at an instant . Get comfortable with this approach here.Tangent slope as instantaneous rate of change Approximating instantaneous rate of change with secant lines Approximating instantaneous rate of change with average rate of change Secant linesGain some experience working with secant lines . This will help us on our journey to find a formal definition for the derivative.Slope of a line secant to a curve Slope of secant lines : arbitrary difference Slope of secant lines : arbitrary point Practice : Secant lines Secant lines ( with simplification ) : arbitrary difference Secant lines ( with simplification ) : arbitrary point Practice : Secant lines ( with simplification ) Slope of secant line challenge Slope of secant line challenge Derivative as a limitThe derivative is actually a special kind of limit ! This is yet another important stop on our continuing journey towards a formal definition of the derivative.Derivative as a limit Derivative as a limit : numerical Practice : Derivative as a limit : numerical Formal definition of derivativeThere are two ways to define the derivative of function f at point x=a . The formal definition is the limit of [ f ( a+h ) -f ( x ) ] /h as h approaches 0 , and the alternative definition is the limit of [ f ( x ) -f ( a ) ] / ( x-a ) as x approaches a . Make introduction with these two definitions.Formal and alternate form of the derivative Derivative of ln ( x ) as a limit Interpreting a limit to find the derivative it describes Practice : Derivative as a limit : algebraic Using the formal definition of derivativeLearn how we can use their formal definition in order to find the derivatives of specific functions . For example , we find the derivative of f ( x ) =x\xc2\xb2 at x=3 , or for any x-value.The derivative of x\xc2\xb2 at x=3 using the formal definition The derivative of x\xc2\xb2 at any point using the formal definition Evaluating a limit expression for the derivative of a linear function Evaluating a limit expression for the derivative of cos ( x ) at a minimum point Evaluating a limit expression for the derivative of function ( graphical ) Tangent lines and rates of change DifferentiabilityThe derivative of a function is n't necessarily defined at every point . Learn about the conditions for the derivative to exist , and specifically about how continuity fits with this story ( spoiler : for a function to be differentiable at a point it must be continuous at that point , but the other way is n't necessary ) .Differentiability at a point : graphical Practice : Differentiability at a point : graphical Differentiability at a point : algebraic ( function is differentiable ) Differentiability at a point : algebraic ( function is n't differentiable ) Practice : Differentiability at a point : algebraic Differentiability at a point ( old ) Derivative as a functionThis may blow your mind , but the derivative of a function is a function in itself ! Get comfortable in thinking about the derivative as a function that is separate from , but tightly related to , its original function.The graphical relationship between a function & its derivative ( part 1 ) The graphical relationship between a function & its derivative ( part 2 ) Matching functions & their derivatives graphically Practice : Visualizing derivatives Identifying functions & their derivatives graphically Matching functions & their derivatives graphically ( old ) Review : Derivative basicsReview your conceptual understanding of derivatives with some challenge problems.Practice : Derivatives basics challenge PracticeBasic differentiation rulesIf you ever tried to find derivatives using their formal definition , you probably know how tedious that may be . Fortunately , we have ways for finding derivatives much quicker , using differentiation rules ! Make your first steps in this fascinating world by working with the more basic rules . For example , the derivative of [ f ( x ) +g ( x ) ] is f ' ( x ) +g ' ( x ) , and the derivative of k\xe2\x8b\x85f ( x ) is k\xe2\x8b\x85f ' ( x ) .The derivative of a constant is 0 Basic differentiation rules Differentiating linear functions Practice : Differentiating linear functions Basic differentiation rules example Practice : Basic differentiation rules Basic differentiation review Derivative notation review Power ruleThe power rule says that the derivative of x\xe2\x81\xbf is n\xe2\x8b\x85x\xe2\x81\xbf\xe2\x81\xbb\xc2\xb9 . It allows us to quickly find the derivative of any polynomial , and it does n't even stop there ! Make introduction with this simple but powerful rule.Power rule Justifying the power rule Proof of power rule for positive integer powers Proof of power rule for square root function Polynomial functions differentiationPut the power rule to use by differentiating various polynomials.Differentiating polynomials Differentiating polynomials example Practice : Polynomial functions differentiation Tangents of polynomials Practice : Tangents of polynomials Differentiating polynomials review Rational functions differentiation ( intro ) Learn how the power rule can be used to differentiate some basic rational functions.Negative powers differentiation Practice : Negative powers differentiation y-intercept of tangent line example Radical functions differentiation ( intro ) Learn how the power rule can be used to differentiate some basic radical functions.Fractional powers differentiation Practice : Fractional powers differentiation Radical functions differentiation intro Practice : Radical functions differentiation intro Power rule review Sine & cosine derivativesThe derivative of sin ( x ) is cos ( x ) and the derivative of cos ( x ) is -sin ( x ) . How convenient ! Practice differentiating functions that include sine and cosine.Derivatives of sin ( x ) , cos ( x ) , tan ( x ) , e\xcb\xa3 & ln ( x ) Sine & cosine differentiation Practice : Sine & cosine differentiation e\xcb\xa3 and ln ( x ) derivativesThe derivative of e\xcb\xa3 is e\xcb\xa3 . That 's pretty amazing . The derivative of ln ( x ) is 1/x , which is just as surprising.Derivatives of sin ( x ) , cos ( x ) , tan ( x ) , e\xcb\xa3 & ln ( x ) Practice : Special derivatives quiz Review : Basic differentiationReview your understanding of basic differentiation rules and your knowledge of the derivatives of common functions with some challenge problems.Practice : Basic differentiation challenge Practice : Power rule challenge Practice : Common derivatives challenge Product ruleThe product rule says that the derivative of the product f ( x ) g ( x ) is f ' ( x ) g ( x ) +f ( x ) g ' ( x ) . This helps us find the derivative of a function which is a product of two other , more basic , functions.Product rule intro Differentiating products Practice : Differentiate products Product rule example : table of values Product rule example : mixed implicit & explicit Practice : Product rule Differentiating products of more than two functions Product rule proof Product rule review Chain ruleThe chain rule says that the derivative of the composite function f ( g ( x ) ) is f ' ( g ( x ) ) \xe2\x8b\x85g ' ( x ) . This helps us find the derivative of a composite function . It may be slightly hard to grasp , but its importance can not be overstated ! Chain rule introduction Differentiating composite functions 1 Differentiating composite functions 2 Differentiating composite functions 3 Chain rule overview Practice : Differentiate composite functions Chain rule example Practice : Chain rule Quotient rule from product & chain rules Chain rule with the power rule Applying the chain rule graphically 1 ( old ) Applying the chain rule graphically 2 ( old ) Applying the chain rule graphically 3 ( old ) Chain rule review Chain rule proofGo `` behind the scenes '' with Sal and learn how the chain rule is proved.Differentiability implies continuity If function u is continuous at x , then \xce\x94u\xe2\x86\x920 As \xce\x94x\xe2\x86\x920 Chain rule proof Quotient ruleThe quotient rule says that the derivative of the quotient f ( x ) /g ( x ) is [ f ' ( x ) g ( x ) -f ( x ) g ' ( x ) ] /g\xc2\xb2 ( x ) . This helps us find the derivative of a function which is a quotient of two other , more basic , functions.Quotient rule from product & chain rules Practice : Differentiate quotients Quotient rule example Practice : Quotient rule Equation of tangent line Equation of normal line Quotient rule review Review : Product , quotient , & chain ruleReview your understanding of the product , quotient , and chain rules with some challenge problems.Practice : Product , quotient , & chain rules challenge Rational functions differentiationSolve problems involving the derivatives of rational functions .
